         <td>178,000</td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table>
      <p>According to a 2020 study by Kiplinger, Delaware had the seventeenth largest number of millionaires per capita in the United States, with a ratio of 6.98 percent, 0.7 percent from 2013 in ration but falling eight places in ranking. Delaware had 25,937 millionaires as of 2020. The median income for all Delaware households as of 2020 was $64,805.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-frank2014_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frank2014-94">[93]</a></sup></p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Peach_delaware.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Peach_delaware.jpg/220px-Peach_delaware.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Peach_delaware.jpg/330px-Peach_delaware.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Peach_delaware.jpg/440px-Peach_delaware.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="401"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Peach_delaware.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i>Picking Peaches in Delaware</i>, from an 1878 issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Harper%27s_Weekly" title="Harper's Weekly">Harper's Weekly</a></i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>Delaware's agricultural output consists of poultry, nursery stock, <a href="/wiki/Soybeans" class="mw-redirect" title="Soybeans">soybeans</a>, dairy products and <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a>.</p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industries">Industries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Industries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <p>As of October&nbsp;2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the state's unemployment rate was 3.7%.<sup id="cite_ref-ktdidit_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ktdidit-95">[94]</a></sup></p>
      <p>The state's largest employers are:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (March 2012)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata"> – <a href="/wiki/Talk:Delaware#largest_employers" title="Talk:Delaware">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup></p>
      <ul>
       <li>government (State of Delaware, New Castle County)</li>
       <li>education (<a href="/wiki/University_of_Delaware" title="University of Delaware">University of Delaware</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Technical_Community_College" title="Delaware Technical Community College">Delaware Technical Community College</a>)</li>
       <li>banking (<a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">Bank of America</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%26T_Bank" title="M&amp;T Bank">M&amp;T Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase" title="JPMorgan Chase">JPMorgan Chase</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">Deutsche Bank</a>)</li>
       <li>chemical, pharmaceutical, technology (<a href="/wiki/DuPont" title="DuPont">DuPont de Nemours Inc.</a>, <a href="/wiki/AstraZeneca" title="AstraZeneca">AstraZeneca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syngenta" title="Syngenta">Syngenta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agilent_Technologies" title="Agilent Technologies">Agilent Technologies</a>)</li>
       <li>healthcare (<a href="/wiki/Christiana_Care_Health_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Christiana Care Health System">Christiana Care Health System</a> (<a href="/wiki/Christiana_Hospital" title="Christiana Hospital">Christiana Hospital</a>), <a href="/wiki/Bayhealth_Medical_Center" title="Bayhealth Medical Center">Bayhealth Medical Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_I._duPont_Hospital_for_Children" class="mw-redirect" title="Alfred I. duPont Hospital for Children">Alfred I. duPont Hospital for Children</a>)</li>
       <li>farming, specifically chicken farming in Sussex County (<a href="/wiki/Perdue_Farms" title="Perdue Farms">Perdue Farms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountaire_Farms" title="Mountaire Farms">Mountaire Farms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allen_Family_Foods" title="Allen Family Foods">Allen Family Foods</a>)</li>
       <li>retail (<a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walgreens" title="Walgreens">Walgreens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acme_Markets" title="Acme Markets">Acme Markets</a>)</li>
      </ul>
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_decline">Industrial decline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Industrial decline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
      <p>Since the mid-2000s, Delaware has seen the departure of the state's automotive manufacturing industry (<a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> <a href="/wiki/Wilmington_Assembly" title="Wilmington Assembly">Wilmington Assembly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chrysler" title="Chrysler">Chrysler</a> <a href="/wiki/Newark_Assembly" title="Newark Assembly">Newark Assembly</a>), the corporate buyout of a major bank holding company (<a href="/wiki/MBNA" title="MBNA">MBNA</a>), the departure of the state's steel industry (<a href="/wiki/Evraz_Claymont_Steel" class="mw-redirect" title="Evraz Claymont Steel">Evraz Claymont Steel</a>), the bankruptcy of a fiber mill (National Vulcanized Fibre),<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> and the diminishing presence of <a href="/wiki/AstraZeneca" title="AstraZeneca">AstraZeneca</a> in Wilmington.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup></p>
      <p>In late 2015, DuPont announced that 1,700 employees, nearly a third of its footprint in Delaware, would be laid off in early 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> The merger of <a href="/wiki/DuPont_(1802%E2%80%932017)" title="DuPont (1802–2017)">E.I. du Pont de Nemours &amp; Co.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dow_Chemical_Company" title="Dow Chemical Company">Dow Chemical Company</a> into <a href="/wiki/DuPont" title="DuPont">DowDuPont</a> took place on September 1, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup></p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Incorporation_in_Delaware">Incorporation in Delaware</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Incorporation in Delaware">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Delaware_General_Corporation_Law" title="Delaware General Corporation Law">Delaware General Corporation Law</a>
      </div>
      <p>More than half of all U.S. publicly traded companies, and 63% of the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a>, are <a href="/wiki/Incorporation_(business)" title="Incorporation (business)">incorporated</a> in Delaware.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> The state's attractiveness as a <a href="/wiki/Corporate_haven" title="Corporate haven">corporate haven</a> is largely because of its business-friendly <a href="/wiki/Delaware_General_Corporation_Law" title="Delaware General Corporation Law">corporation law</a>. <a href="/wiki/Franchise_tax" title="Franchise tax">Franchise taxes</a> on Delaware corporations supply about a fifth of the state's revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-DEFiscalNotebook_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DEFiscalNotebook-105">[104]</a></sup> Although "USA (Delaware)" ranked as the world's most opaque jurisdiction on the <a href="/wiki/Tax_Justice_Network" title="Tax Justice Network">Tax Justice Network</a>'s 2009 Financial Secrecy Index,<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> the same group's 2011 Index ranks the U.S. fifth and does not specify Delaware.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> In Delaware, there are more than a million registered corporations,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> meaning there are more corporations than people.</p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_and_drink">Food and drink</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Food and drink">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <p><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Delaware_Code/Title_4/Chapter_7" class="extiw" title="s:Delaware Code/Title 4/Chapter 7">Title 4, chapter 7 of the Delaware Code</a> stipulates that alcoholic liquor be sold only in specifically licensed establishments, and only between 9:00<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>a.m. and 1:00<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>a.m.<sup id="cite_ref-delcode4-8_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-delcode4-8-109">[108]</a></sup> Until 2003, Delaware was among the several states enforcing <a href="/wiki/Blue_law" title="Blue law">blue laws</a> and banned the sale of liquor on Sunday.<sup id="cite_ref-nathans2011_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nathans2011-110">[109]</a></sup></p>
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers">Newspapers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Newspapers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <p>Two <a href="/wiki/Daily_newspaper" class="mw-redirect" title="Daily newspaper">daily newspapers</a> are based in Delaware, the <i><a href="/wiki/Delaware_State_News" title="Delaware State News">Delaware State News</a></i>, based in Dover and covering the two southern counties, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_News_Journal" title="The News Journal">The News Journal</a></i> covering Wilmington and northern Delaware. The state is also served by <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Delaware" title="List of newspapers in Delaware">several weekly, monthly and online publications</a>.</p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <p>No standalone television stations are based solely in Delaware. The northern part of the state is served by network stations in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> and the southern part by network stations in <a href="/wiki/Salisbury,_Maryland" title="Salisbury, Maryland">Salisbury, Maryland</a>. Philadelphia's <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> affiliate, <a href="/wiki/WPVI-TV" title="WPVI-TV">WPVI-TV</a>, maintains a news bureau in downtown Wilmington. Salisbury's <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> affiliate, <a href="/wiki/WBOC-TV" title="WBOC-TV">WBOC-TV</a>, maintains bureaus in Dover and Milton. Three Philadelphia-market stations—<a href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Broadcasting Service">PBS</a> member <a href="/wiki/WHYY-TV" title="WHYY-TV">WHYY-TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ion_Television" title="Ion Television">Ion</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/WPPX" class="mw-redirect" title="WPPX">WPPX</a>, and <a href="/wiki/MeTV" title="MeTV">MeTV</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/WDPN-TV" title="WDPN-TV">WDPN-TV</a>—all have Wilmington as their <a href="/wiki/City_of_license" title="City of license">city of license</a>, but maintain transmitters at the market antenna farm in <a href="/wiki/Roxborough,_Philadelphia" title="Roxborough, Philadelphia">Roxborough</a> and do not produce any Delaware-centric programming.</p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_radio_stations_in_Delaware" title="List of radio stations in Delaware">List of radio stations in Delaware</a>
      </div>
      <p>There are a numerous radio stations licensed in Delaware. <a href="/wiki/WDEL_1150AM" class="mw-redirect" title="WDEL 1150AM">WDEL 1150AM</a>, <a href="/wiki/WHGE-LP" title="WHGE-LP">WHGE</a>-LP 95.3 FM, WILM 1450 AM, <a href="/wiki/WJBR-FM" title="WJBR-FM">WJBR-FM 99.5</a>, <a href="/wiki/WMPH" title="WMPH">WMPH</a> 91.7 FM, <a href="/wiki/WSTW" title="WSTW">WSTW</a> 93.7 FM, <a href="/wiki/WTMC" title="WTMC">WTMC</a> 1380 AM and <a href="/wiki/WWTX" title="WWTX">WWTX</a> 1290AM are licensed from Wilmington. <a href="/wiki/WRDX" title="WRDX">WRDX</a> 92.9 FM is licensed from Smyrna. <a href="/wiki/WDOV" title="WDOV">WDOV</a> 1410AM, <a href="/wiki/WDSD" title="WDSD">WDSD</a> 94.7 FM and WRTX 91.7 FM are licensed from Dover.</p>
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rehoboth_Beach_looking_north_at_Delaware_Avenue_August_2021.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Rehoboth_Beach_looking_north_at_Delaware_Avenue_August_2021.jpeg/200px-Rehoboth_Beach_looking_north_at_Delaware_Avenue_August_2021.jpeg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Rehoboth_Beach_looking_north_at_Delaware_Avenue_August_2021.jpeg/300px-Rehoboth_Beach_looking_north_at_Delaware_Avenue_August_2021.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Rehoboth_Beach_looking_north_at_Delaware_Avenue_August_2021.jpeg/400px-Rehoboth_Beach_looking_north_at_Delaware_Avenue_August_2021.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rehoboth_Beach_looking_north_at_Delaware_Avenue_August_2021.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Rehoboth Beach is a popular vacation spot during the summer months.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Fort_Delaware_LOC_384066pu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Fort_Delaware_LOC_384066pu.jpg/200px-Fort_Delaware_LOC_384066pu.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Fort_Delaware_LOC_384066pu.jpg/300px-Fort_Delaware_LOC_384066pu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Fort_Delaware_LOC_384066pu.jpg/400px-Fort_Delaware_LOC_384066pu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3867" data-file-height="3025"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Fort_Delaware_LOC_384066pu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Fort_Delaware_State_Park" title="Fort Delaware State Park">Fort Delaware State Park</a> on Pea Patch Island is a popular spot during the spring and summer. A ferry takes visitors to the fort from nearby <a href="/wiki/Delaware_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Delaware City">Delaware City</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>Delaware is home to <a href="/wiki/First_State_National_Historical_Park" title="First State National Historical Park">First State National Historical Park</a>, a <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a> unit composed of historic sites across the state including the <a href="/wiki/New_Castle_Court_House_Museum" title="New Castle Court House Museum">New Castle Court House, Green, and Sheriff's House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dover_Green_Historic_District" title="Dover Green Historic District">Dover Green</a>, Beaver Valley, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Christina" title="Fort Christina">Fort Christina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holy_Trinity_Church_(Old_Swedes)" title="Holy Trinity Church (Old Swedes)">Old Swedes' Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Dickinson_House" title="John Dickinson House">John Dickinson Plantation</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ryves_Holt_House" title="Ryves Holt House">Ryves Holt House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> Delaware has several <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Delaware" title="List of museums in Delaware">museums</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:National_Wildlife_Refuges_in_Delaware" title="Category:National Wildlife Refuges in Delaware">wildlife refuges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Parks_in_Delaware" title="Category:Parks in Delaware">parks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Houses_in_Delaware" title="Category:Houses in Delaware">houses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Lighthouses_in_Delaware" title="Category:Lighthouses in Delaware">lighthouses</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Category:National_Register_of_Historic_Places_in_Delaware" title="Category:National Register of Historic Places in Delaware">historic places</a>.</p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rehoboth_Beach,_Delaware" title="Rehoboth Beach, Delaware">Rehoboth Beach</a>, together with the towns of <a href="/wiki/Lewes,_Delaware" title="Lewes, Delaware">Lewes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dewey_Beach,_Delaware" title="Dewey Beach, Delaware">Dewey Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bethany_Beach,_Delaware" title="Bethany Beach, Delaware">Bethany Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Bethany,_Delaware" title="South Bethany, Delaware">South Bethany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fenwick_Island,_Delaware" title="Fenwick Island, Delaware">Fenwick Island</a>, comprise <a href="/wiki/Delaware_beaches" class="mw-redirect" title="Delaware beaches">Delaware's beach resorts</a>. Rehoboth Beach often bills itself as "The Nation's Summer Capital" because it is a frequent summer vacation destination for Washington, D.C., residents as well as visitors from Maryland, Virginia, and in lesser numbers, Pennsylvania. Vacationers are drawn for many reasons, including the town's charm, artistic appeal, nightlife, and tax-free shopping. According to SeaGrant Delaware, the Delaware beaches generate $6.9<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>billion annually and over $711<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>million in tax revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup></p>
      <p>Delaware is home to several festivals, fairs, and events. Some of the more notable festivals are the Riverfest held in <a href="/wiki/Seaford,_Delaware" title="Seaford, Delaware">Seaford</a>, the World Championship <a href="/wiki/Punkin_Chunkin#World_Championship_Punkin_Chunkin" class="mw-redirect" title="Punkin Chunkin">Punkin Chunkin</a> formerly held at various locations throughout the state since 1986, the Rehoboth Beach Chocolate Festival, the Bethany Beach Jazz Funeral to mark the end of summer, the Apple Scrapple Festival held in <a href="/wiki/Bridgeville,_Delaware" title="Bridgeville, Delaware">Bridgeville</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Clifford_Brown" title="Clifford Brown">Clifford Brown</a> Jazz Festival in Wilmington, the Rehoboth Beach Jazz Festival, the Sea Witch Halloween Festival and Parade in Rehoboth Beach, the Rehoboth Beach Independent Film Festival, the Nanticoke Indian Pow Wow in <a href="/wiki/Oak_Orchard,_Delaware" title="Oak Orchard, Delaware">Oak Orchard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Firefly_Music_Festival" title="Firefly Music Festival">Firefly Music Festival</a>, and the Return Day Parade held after every election in <a href="/wiki/Georgetown,_Delaware" title="Georgetown, Delaware">Georgetown</a>.</p>
      <p>In 2015, tourism in Delaware generated $3.1<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>billion, which makes up five percent of the state's GDP. Delaware saw 8.5<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>million visitors in 2015, with the tourism industry employing 41,730 people, making it the 4th largest private employer in the state. Major origin markets for Delaware tourists include <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, New York City, Washington, D.C., and <a href="/wiki/Harrisburg,_Pennsylvania" title="Harrisburg, Pennsylvania">Harrisburg</a>, with 97% of tourists arriving to the state by car and 75% of tourists coming from a distance of 200 miles (320&nbsp;km) or less.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup></p>
      <p>Delaware is also home to two large sporting venues. <a href="/wiki/Dover_International_Speedway" title="Dover International Speedway">Dover International Speedway</a> is a race track in Dover, and <a href="/wiki/Daniel_S._Frawley_Stadium" title="Daniel S. Frawley Stadium">Frawley Stadium</a> in Wilmington is the home of the <a href="/wiki/Wilmington_Blue_Rocks" title="Wilmington Blue Rocks">Wilmington Blue Rocks</a>, a Minor League Baseball team.</p>
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:UDel_Memorial_and_Magnolia_Circle.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/UDel_Memorial_and_Magnolia_Circle.JPG/220px-UDel_Memorial_and_Magnolia_Circle.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/UDel_Memorial_and_Magnolia_Circle.JPG/330px-UDel_Memorial_and_Magnolia_Circle.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/UDel_Memorial_and_Magnolia_Circle.JPG/440px-UDel_Memorial_and_Magnolia_Circle.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2608" data-file-height="1952"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:UDel_Memorial_and_Magnolia_Circle.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>University of Delaware
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p><br>In the early 1920s, <a href="/wiki/Pierre_S._du_Pont" title="Pierre S. du Pont">Pierre S. du Pont</a> served as president of the state board of education. At the time, state law prohibited money raised from white taxpayers from being used to support the state's schools for black children. Appalled by the condition of the black schools, du Pont donated four million dollars to construct 86 new school buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup></p>
      <p>Delaware was the origin of <i><a href="/wiki/Belton_v._Gebhart" class="mw-redirect" title="Belton v. Gebhart">Belton v. Gebhart</a></i> (1952), one of the four cases which were combined into <i><a href="/wiki/Brown_v._Board_of_Education" title="Brown v. Board of Education">Brown v. Board of Education</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a> decision that led to the end of officially <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation" title="Racial segregation">segregated</a> public schools. Significantly, <i>Belton</i> was the only case in which the state court found for the plaintiffs, thereby ruling that segregation is unconstitutional.</p>
      <p>Unlike many states, Delaware's educational system is centralized in a state Superintendent of Education, with local school boards retaining control over taxation and some curriculum decisions. This centralized system, combined with the small size of the state, likely contributed to Delaware becoming the first state, after completion of a three-year, $30<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>million program ending in 1999, to wire every K-12 classroom in the state to the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup></p>
      <p>As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the Delaware Department of Education had authorized the founding of 25 charter schools in the state, one of them being <a href="/wiki/Single-sex_education" title="Single-sex education">all-girls</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dobo20110612_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dobo20110612-116">[115]</a></sup></p>
      <p>All teachers in the State's public school districts are unionized.<sup id="cite_ref-dobo2012_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dobo2012-117">[116]</a></sup> As of January 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, none of the State's charter schools are members of a teachers <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dobo2012_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dobo2012-117">[116]</a></sup> One of the State's teachers' unions is Delaware State Education Association (DSEA), whose President as of January&nbsp;2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> is Frederika Jenner.<sup id="cite_ref-dobo2012_117-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dobo2012-117">[116]</a></sup></p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Delaware_College_of_Art_and_Design" title="Delaware College of Art and Design">Delaware College of Art and Design</a></li>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Delaware_State_University" title="Delaware State University">Delaware State University</a></li>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Delaware_Technical_%26_Community_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Delaware Technical &amp; Community College">Delaware Technical &amp; Community College</a></li>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Drexel_University" title="Drexel University">Drexel University</a> at Wilmington</li>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Goldey-Beacom_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Goldey-Beacom College">Goldey-Beacom College</a></li>
       <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Delaware" title="University of Delaware">University of Delaware</a>—Ranked 63rd in the U.S. and in top 201–250 in the world (<a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a> 2018)</li>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wesley_College_(Delaware)" title="Wesley College (Delaware)">Wesley College</a></li>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Widener_University_School_of_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Widener University School of Law">Widener University School of Law</a></li>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wilmington_University" title="Wilmington University">Wilmington University</a></li>
      </ul>
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:1969_Delaware_license_plate_000000_sample.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/69/1969_Delaware_license_plate_000000_sample.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="100" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="100"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:1969_Delaware_license_plate_000000_sample.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Delaware's <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_registration_plates_of_Delaware" title="Vehicle registration plates of Delaware">license plate</a> design, introduced in 1959, is the longest-running one in U.S. history.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>The transportation system in Delaware is under the governance and supervision of the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Department_of_Transportation" title="Delaware Department of Transportation">Delaware Department of Transportation</a>, also known as "DelDOT".<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> Funding for DelDOT projects is drawn, in part, from the Delaware Transportation Trust Fund, established in 1987 to help stabilize transportation funding; the availability of the Trust led to a gradual separation of DelDOT operations from other Delaware state operations.<sup id="cite_ref-montgomery2012nj_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-montgomery2012nj-121">[120]</a></sup> DelDOT manages programs such as a Delaware <a href="/wiki/Adopt-a-Highway" title="Adopt-a-Highway">Adopt-a-Highway</a> program, major road route snow removal, traffic control infrastructure (signs and signals), toll road management, Delaware <a href="/wiki/Division_of_Motor_Vehicles" class="mw-redirect" title="Division of Motor Vehicles">Division of Motor Vehicles</a>, the Delaware Transit Corporation (branded as "<a href="/wiki/DART_First_State" title="DART First State">DART First State</a>", the state government public transportation organization), among others. In 2009, DelDOT maintained 13,507 lane-miles, totaling 89 percent of the state's public roadway system, the rest being under the supervision of individual municipalities. This far exceeds the national average (20 percent) for state department of transportation maintenance responsibility.<sup id="cite_ref-deldotfactbook_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deldotfactbook-122">[121]</a></sup></p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Delaware_State_Route_System" title="Delaware State Route System">Delaware State Route System</a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:DE_1_NB_from_DE_299_overpass.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/DE_1_NB_from_DE_299_overpass.jpeg/220px-DE_1_NB_from_DE_299_overpass.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/DE_1_NB_from_DE_299_overpass.jpeg/330px-DE_1_NB_from_DE_299_overpass.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/DE_1_NB_from_DE_299_overpass.jpeg/440px-DE_1_NB_from_DE_299_overpass.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:DE_1_NB_from_DE_299_overpass.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Delaware_Route_1" title="Delaware Route 1">Delaware Route&nbsp;1</a> (DE<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>1) is a partial <a href="/wiki/Toll_road" title="Toll road">toll road</a> linking <a href="/wiki/Fenwick_Island,_Delaware" title="Fenwick Island, Delaware">Fenwick Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_Delaware" title="Wilmington, Delaware">Wilmington</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>One major branch of the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Interstate_Highway_System" title="Interstate Highway System">Interstate Highway System</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Delaware" title="Interstate 95 in Delaware">Interstate<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>95</a> (I-95), crosses Delaware southwest-to-northeast across New Castle County. In addition to I-95, there are six <a href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_System" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Highway System">U.S. highways</a> that serve Delaware: <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_9_in_Delaware" title="U.S. Route 9 in Delaware">U.S.<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>9</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_13_in_Delaware" title="U.S. Route 13 in Delaware">U.S.<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>13</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_40_in_Delaware" title="U.S. Route 40 in Delaware">U.S.<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>40</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_113_in_Delaware" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Route 113 in Delaware">U.S.<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>113</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_202_in_Delaware" title="U.S. Route 202 in Delaware">U.S.<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>202</a>, and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_301_in_Delaware" title="U.S. Route 301 in Delaware">U.S.<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>301</a>. There are also several state highways that cross the state of Delaware; a few of them include <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Route_1" title="Delaware Route 1">DE<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Route_9" title="Delaware Route 9">DE<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>9</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Route_404" title="Delaware Route 404">DE<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>404</a>. U.S.<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>13 and DE<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>1 are primary north–south highways connecting Wilmington and Pennsylvania with Maryland, with DE<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>1 serving as the main route between Wilmington and the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_beaches" class="mw-redirect" title="Delaware beaches">Delaware beaches</a>. DE<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>9 is a north–south highway connecting Dover and Wilmington via a scenic route along the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Bay" title="Delaware Bay">Delaware Bay</a>. U.S.<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>40 is a primary east–west route, connecting Maryland with New Jersey. DE<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>404 is another primary east–west highway connecting the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge" title="Chesapeake Bay Bridge">Chesapeake Bay Bridge</a> in Maryland with the Delaware beaches. The state also operates three toll highways, the Delaware Turnpike, which is I-95, between Maryland and New Castle; the Korean War Veterans Memorial Highway, which is DE<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>1, between Wilmington and Dover; and the U.S. 301 toll road between the Maryland border and DE<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>1 in New Castle County.</p>
      <p>A bicycle route, <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Bicycle_Route_1" title="Delaware Bicycle Route 1">Delaware Bicycle Route&nbsp;1</a>, spans the north–south length of the state from the Maryland border in <a href="/wiki/Fenwick_Island,_Delaware" title="Fenwick Island, Delaware">Fenwick Island</a> to the Pennsylvania border north of <a href="/wiki/Montchanin,_Delaware" title="Montchanin, Delaware">Montchanin</a>. It is the first of several signed bike routes planned in Delaware.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup></p>
      <p>Delaware has about 1,450 bridges, 95 percent of which are under the supervision of DelDOT. About 30 percent of all Delaware bridges were built before 1950, and about 60 percent of the number are included in the <a href="/wiki/National_Bridge_Inventory" title="National Bridge Inventory">National Bridge Inventory</a>. Some bridges not under DelDOT supervision includes the four bridges on the Chesapeake and Delaware Canal, which are under the jurisdiction of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Army_Corps_of_Engineers" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Army Corps of Engineers">U.S. Army Corps of Engineers</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Memorial_Bridge" title="Delaware Memorial Bridge">Delaware Memorial Bridge</a>, which is under the bi-state <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River_and_Bay_Authority" title="Delaware River and Bay Authority">Delaware River and Bay Authority</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
      <p>It has been noted that the <a href="/wiki/Tar_and_chip" class="mw-redirect" title="Tar and chip">tar and chip</a> composition of secondary roads in Sussex County makes them more prone to <a href="/wiki/Road_surface#Surface_deterioration" title="Road surface">deterioration</a> than are the <a href="/wiki/Asphalt_concrete" title="Asphalt concrete">asphalt</a> roadways in almost the rest of the state.<sup id="cite_ref-nj20110417_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nj20110417-124">[123]</a></sup> Among these roads, Sussex (county road) 236 is among the most problematic.<sup id="cite_ref-nj20110417_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nj20110417-124">[123]</a></sup></p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ferries">Ferries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Ferries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MV_Delaware_DEE1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/MV_Delaware_DEE1.jpg/220px-MV_Delaware_DEE1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="98" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/MV_Delaware_DEE1.jpg/330px-MV_Delaware_DEE1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/MV_Delaware_DEE1.jpg/440px-MV_Delaware_DEE1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5394" data-file-height="2396"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MV_Delaware_DEE1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Cape May–Lewes Ferry
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>Three ferries operate in the state of Delaware:</p>
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Cape_May%E2%80%93Lewes_Ferry" title="Cape May–Lewes Ferry">Cape May–Lewes Ferry</a> crosses the mouth of Delaware Bay between Lewes, Delaware, and <a href="/wiki/Cape_May,_New_Jersey" title="Cape May, New Jersey">Cape May, New Jersey</a>.</li>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Woodland_Ferry" title="Woodland Ferry">Woodland Ferry</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Cable_ferry" title="Cable ferry">cable ferry</a>) crosses the <a href="/wiki/Nanticoke_River" title="Nanticoke River">Nanticoke River</a> southwest of <a href="/wiki/Seaford,_Delaware" title="Seaford, Delaware">Seaford</a>.</li>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Forts_Ferry_Crossing" title="Forts Ferry Crossing">Forts Ferry Crossing</a> connects <a href="/wiki/Delaware_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Delaware City">Delaware City</a> with <a href="/wiki/Fort_Delaware" title="Fort Delaware">Fort Delaware</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fort_Mott_(New_Jersey)" title="Fort Mott (New Jersey)">Fort Mott</a>, New Jersey.</li>
      </ul>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_and_bus">Rail and bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Rail and bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Wilmington_Station_from_parking_garage,_July_2014.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Wilmington_Station_from_parking_garage%2C_July_2014.JPG/220px-Wilmington_Station_from_parking_garage%2C_July_2014.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Wilmington_Station_from_parking_garage%2C_July_2014.JPG/330px-Wilmington_Station_from_parking_garage%2C_July_2014.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Wilmington_Station_from_parking_garage%2C_July_2014.JPG/440px-Wilmington_Station_from_parking_garage%2C_July_2014.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Wilmington_Station_from_parking_garage,_July_2014.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Wilmington Station
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> has two stations in Delaware along the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor" title="Northeast Corridor">Northeast Corridor</a>; the relatively quiet <a href="/wiki/Newark_Rail_Station_(Delaware)" class="mw-redirect" title="Newark Rail Station (Delaware)">Newark Rail Station</a> in Newark, and the busier <a href="/wiki/Wilmington_station_(Delaware)" title="Wilmington station (Delaware)">Wilmington Rail Station</a> in Wilmington. The Northeast Corridor is also served by <a href="/wiki/SEPTA" title="SEPTA">SEPTA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Wilmington/Newark_Line" title="Wilmington/Newark Line">Wilmington/Newark Line</a> of <a href="/wiki/SEPTA_Regional_Rail" title="SEPTA Regional Rail">Regional Rail</a>, which serves <a href="/wiki/Claymont_station" title="Claymont station">Claymont</a>, Wilmington, <a href="/wiki/Churchmans_Crossing,_Delaware" class="mw-redirect" title="Churchmans Crossing, Delaware">Churchmans Crossing</a>, and Newark.</p>
      <p>Two <a href="/wiki/Class_I_railroad" class="mw-redirect" title="Class I railroad">Class I railroads</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Southern" class="mw-redirect" title="Norfolk Southern">Norfolk Southern</a> and <a href="/wiki/CSX" class="mw-redirect" title="CSX">CSX</a>, provide freight rail service in northern New Castle County. Norfolk Southern provides freight service along the Northeast Corridor and to industrial areas in <a href="/wiki/Edgemoor,_Delaware" title="Edgemoor, Delaware">Edgemoor</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Castle,_Delaware" title="New Castle, Delaware">New Castle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Delaware_City,_Delaware" title="Delaware City, Delaware">Delaware City</a>. CSX's <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Subdivision" title="Philadelphia Subdivision">Philadelphia Subdivision</a> passes through northern New Castle County parallel to the Amtrak Northeast Corridor. Multiple <a href="/wiki/Short-line_railroad" class="mw-redirect" title="Short-line railroad">short-line railroads</a> provide freight service in Delaware. The <a href="/wiki/Delmarva_Central_Railroad" title="Delmarva Central Railroad">Delmarva Central Railroad</a> operates the most trackage of the short-line railroads, running from an interchange with Norfolk Southern in <a href="/wiki/Porter,_Delaware" title="Porter, Delaware">Porter</a> south through <a href="/wiki/Dover,_Delaware" title="Dover, Delaware">Dover</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harrington,_Delaware" title="Harrington, Delaware">Harrington</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Seaford,_Delaware" title="Seaford, Delaware">Seaford</a> to <a href="/wiki/Delmar,_Delaware" title="Delmar, Delaware">Delmar</a>, with another line running from Harrington to <a href="/wiki/Frankford,_Delaware" title="Frankford, Delaware">Frankford</a> and branches from <a href="/wiki/Ellendale,_Delaware" title="Ellendale, Delaware">Ellendale</a> to <a href="/wiki/Milton,_Delaware" title="Milton, Delaware">Milton</a> and from <a href="/wiki/Georgetown,_Delaware" title="Georgetown, Delaware">Georgetown</a> to <a href="/wiki/Gravel_Hill,_Delaware" title="Gravel Hill, Delaware">Gravel Hill</a>. The Delmarva Central Railroad connects with the <a href="/wiki/Maryland_and_Delaware_Railroad" title="Maryland and Delaware Railroad">Maryland and Delaware Railroad</a>, which serves local customers in Sussex County.<sup id="cite_ref-dcr_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dcr-125">[124]</a></sup> CSX connects with the freight/<a href="/wiki/Heritage_railroad" class="mw-redirect" title="Heritage railroad">heritage</a> operation, the <a href="/wiki/Wilmington_and_Western_Railroad" title="Wilmington and Western Railroad">Wilmington and Western Railroad</a>, based in Wilmington and the <a href="/wiki/East_Penn_Railroad" title="East Penn Railroad">East Penn Railroad</a>, which operates a line from Wilmington to <a href="/wiki/Coatesville,_Pennsylvania" title="Coatesville, Pennsylvania">Coatesville, Pennsylvania</a>.</p>
      <p>The last north–south passenger trains through the main part of Delaware was the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Railroad" title="Pennsylvania Railroad">Pennsylvania Railroad</a>'s local Wilmington-Delmar train in 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> This was a successor to the <i><a href="/wiki/Del-Mar-Va_Express" title="Del-Mar-Va Express">Del-Mar-Va Express</a></i> and <i>Cavalier</i>, which had run from Philadelphia through the state's interior, to the end of the Delmarva Peninsula until the mid-1950s.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup></p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/DART_First_State" title="DART First State">DART First State</a> public transportation system was named "Most Outstanding Public Transportation System" in 2003 by the <a href="/wiki/American_Public_Transportation_Association" title="American Public Transportation Association">American Public Transportation Association</a>. Coverage of the system is broad within northern New Castle County with close association to major highways in Kent and Sussex counties. The system includes bus, subsidized passenger rail operated by Philadelphia transit agency SEPTA, and subsidized taxi and <a href="/wiki/Paratransit" title="Paratransit">paratransit</a> modes. The paratransit system, consisting of a statewide door-to-door bus service for the elderly and disabled, has been described by a Delaware state report as "the most generous paratransit system in the United States".<sup id="cite_ref-montgomery2012nj_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-montgomery2012nj-121">[120]</a></sup> As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, fees for the paratransit service have not changed since 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-montgomery2012nj_121-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-montgomery2012nj-121">[120]</a></sup></p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Aviation_in_Delaware" title="Aviation in Delaware">Aviation in Delaware</a>
      </div>
      <p>As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there is no scheduled air service from any Delaware airport, as has been the case in various years since 1991. Various airlines had served <a href="/wiki/Wilmington_Airport_(Delaware)" title="Wilmington Airport (Delaware)">Wilmington Airport</a>, the latest departure being <a href="/wiki/Frontier_Airlines" title="Frontier Airlines">Frontier Airlines</a> in April 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup></p>
      <p>Delaware is centrally situated in the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_megalopolis" title="Northeast megalopolis">Northeast megalopolis</a> region of cities along <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95" title="Interstate 95">I-95</a>. Therefore, Delaware <a href="/wiki/Commercial_airline" class="mw-redirect" title="Commercial airline">commercial airline</a> passengers most frequently use <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_International_Airport" title="Philadelphia International Airport">Philadelphia International Airport</a> (PHL), <a href="/wiki/Baltimore-Washington_International_Thurgood_Marshall_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Baltimore-Washington International Thurgood Marshall Airport">Baltimore-Washington International Thurgood Marshall Airport</a> (BWI) and <a href="/wiki/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Dulles International Airport">Washington Dulles International Airport</a> (IAD) for domestic and international transit. Residents of Sussex County will also use <a href="/wiki/Wicomico_Regional_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Wicomico Regional Airport">Wicomico Regional Airport</a> (SBY), as it is located less than 10 miles (16&nbsp;km) from the Delaware border. <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_City_International_Airport" title="Atlantic City International Airport">Atlantic City International Airport</a> (ACY), <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark Liberty International Airport</a> (EWR), and <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan_Washington_National_Airport" title="Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport">Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport</a> (DCA) are also within a 100-mile (160&nbsp;km) radius of New Castle County.</p>
      <p>Other general aviation airports in Delaware include <a href="/wiki/Summit_Airport_(Delaware)" title="Summit Airport (Delaware)">Summit Airport</a> near <a href="/wiki/Middletown,_Delaware" title="Middletown, Delaware">Middletown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Airpark" title="Delaware Airpark">Delaware Airpark</a> near <a href="/wiki/Cheswold,_Delaware" title="Cheswold, Delaware">Cheswold</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Coastal_Airport" title="Delaware Coastal Airport">Delaware Coastal Airport</a> near <a href="/wiki/Georgetown,_Delaware" title="Georgetown, Delaware">Georgetown</a>.</p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Dover_Air_Force_Base" title="Dover Air Force Base">Dover Air Force Base</a>, one of the largest in the country, is home to the <a href="/wiki/436th_Airlift_Wing" title="436th Airlift Wing">436th Airlift Wing</a> and the <a href="/wiki/512th_Airlift_Wing" title="512th Airlift Wing">512th Airlift Wing</a>. In addition to its other responsibilities in the <a href="/wiki/Air_Mobility_Command" title="Air Mobility Command">Air Mobility Command</a>, it serves as the entry point and <a href="/wiki/Mortuary" class="mw-redirect" title="Mortuary">mortuary</a> for U.S. military personnel (and some civilians) who die overseas.</p>
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_government">Law and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Law and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
      <p>Delaware's fourth and current constitution, adopted in 1897, provides for executive, judicial and legislative branches.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup></p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislative_branch">Legislative branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Legislative branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Delaware_State_Capitol.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Delaware_State_Capitol.jpg/220px-Delaware_State_Capitol.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Delaware_State_Capitol.jpg/330px-Delaware_State_Capitol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Delaware_State_Capitol.jpg/440px-Delaware_State_Capitol.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Delaware_State_Capitol.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Delaware_General_Assembly" title="Delaware General Assembly">Delaware General Assembly</a> meets in the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_State_Capitol" class="mw-redirect" title="Delaware State Capitol">Legislative Hall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dover,_Delaware" title="Dover, Delaware">Dover</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Delaware_General_Assembly" title="Delaware General Assembly">Delaware General Assembly</a> consists of a <a href="/wiki/Delaware_House_of_Representatives" title="Delaware House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a> with 41 members and a <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Senate" title="Delaware Senate">Senate</a> with 21 members. It sits in Dover, the state capital. Representatives are elected to two-year terms, while senators are elected to four-year terms. The Senate confirms judicial and other nominees appointed by the governor.</p>
      <p>Delaware's U.S. Senators are <a href="/wiki/Tom_Carper" title="Tom Carper">Tom Carper</a> (Democrat) and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Coons" title="Chris Coons">Chris Coons</a> (Democrat). Delaware's single U.S. Representative is <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Blunt_Rochester" title="Lisa Blunt Rochester">Lisa Blunt Rochester</a> (Democrat).</p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_branch">Judicial branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Judicial branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <p>The Delaware Constitution establishes a number of courts:</p>
      <ul>
       <li>The <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Supreme_Court" title="Delaware Supreme Court">Delaware Supreme Court</a> is the state's highest court.</li>
       <li>The <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Superior_Court" title="Delaware Superior Court">Delaware Superior Court</a> is the state's trial court of general jurisdiction.</li>
       <li>The <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Court_of_Chancery" title="Delaware Court of Chancery">Delaware Court of Chancery</a> deals primarily in corporate disputes.</li>
       <li>The <a href="/wiki/Family_court#In_the_United_States" title="Family court">Family Court</a> handles domestic and custody matters.</li>
       <li>The <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Court_of_Common_Pleas" title="Delaware Court of Common Pleas">Delaware Court of Common Pleas</a> has jurisdiction over a limited class of civil and criminal matters.</li>
      </ul>
      <p>Minor non-constitutional courts include the <a href="/wiki/Justice_of_the_Peace" class="mw-redirect" title="Justice of the Peace">Justice of the Peace</a> Courts and Aldermen's Courts.</p>
      <p>Significantly, Delaware has one of the few remaining Courts of <a href="/wiki/Court_of_equity" title="Court of equity">Chancery</a> in the nation, which has jurisdiction over <a href="/wiki/Equity_(law)" title="Equity (law)">equity</a> cases, the vast majority of which are corporate disputes, many relating to <a href="/wiki/Mergers_and_acquisitions" title="Mergers and acquisitions">mergers and acquisitions</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Court_of_Chancery" title="Delaware Court of Chancery">Court of Chancery</a> and the Delaware Supreme Court have developed a worldwide reputation for rendering concise opinions concerning <a href="/wiki/Corporate_law" title="Corporate law">corporate law</a> which generally (but not always) grant broad discretion to corporate boards of directors and officers. In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_General_Corporation_Law" title="Delaware General Corporation Law">Delaware General Corporation Law</a>, which forms the basis of the Courts' opinions, is widely regarded as giving great flexibility to corporations to manage their affairs. For these reasons, Delaware is considered to have the most business-friendly legal system in the United States; therefore a great number of companies are <a href="/wiki/Incorporated_in_Delaware" class="mw-redirect" title="Incorporated in Delaware">incorporated in Delaware</a>, including 60% of the companies listed on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-divcorpabout_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-divcorpabout-132">[131]</a></sup></p>
      <p>Delaware was the last U.S. state to use <a href="/wiki/Judicial_corporal_punishment" title="Judicial corporal punishment">judicial corporal punishment</a>, in 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup></p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive_branch">Executive branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Executive branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Delaware" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Governors of Delaware">List of Governors of Delaware</a>
      </div>
      <p>The executive branch is headed by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Delaware" class="mw-redirect" title="Governor of Delaware">Governor of Delaware</a>. The present governor is <a href="/wiki/John_C._Carney_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="John C. Carney Jr.">John Carney</a> (Democrat), who took office January 17, 2017. The lieutenant governor is <a href="/wiki/Bethany_Hall-Long" title="Bethany Hall-Long">Bethany Hall-Long</a>. The governor presents a "<a href="/wiki/State_of_the_State" class="mw-redirect" title="State of the State">State of the State</a>" speech to a <a href="/wiki/Joint_session" title="Joint session">joint session</a> of the Delaware legislature annually.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup></p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Counties_2">Counties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Counties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <p>Delaware is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Delaware" title="List of counties in Delaware">three counties</a>; from north to south they are <a href="/wiki/New_Castle_County,_Delaware" title="New Castle County, Delaware">New Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kent_County,_Delaware" title="Kent County, Delaware">Kent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sussex_County,_Delaware" title="Sussex County, Delaware">Sussex</a>. This is the fewest among all states. Each county elects its own legislative body (known in New Castle and Sussex counties as <b>County Council</b>, and in Kent County as <b>Levy Court</b>), which deal primarily in zoning and development issues. Most functions which are handled on a county-by-county basis in other states—such as court and law enforcement—have been centralized in Delaware, leading to a significant concentration of power in the Delaware state government. The counties were historically divided into <a href="/wiki/Hundred_(country_subdivision)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hundred (country subdivision)">hundreds</a>, which were used as tax reporting and voting districts until the 1960s, but now serve no administrative role, their only current official legal use being in real estate title descriptions.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup></p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Delaware" title="Politics of Delaware">Politics of Delaware</a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Joe_Biden_presidential_portrait_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Joe_Biden_presidential_portrait_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Joe_Biden_presidential_portrait_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Joe_Biden_presidential_portrait_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Joe_Biden_presidential_portrait_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Joe_Biden_presidential_portrait_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Joe_Biden_presidential_portrait_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1491" data-file-height="1988"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Joe_Biden_presidential_portrait_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a>, the 46th president of the United States and a U.S. senator for Delaware from 1973 to 2009.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>The Democratic Party holds a <a href="/wiki/Pluralism_(political_theory)" title="Pluralism (political theory)">plurality</a> of registrations in Delaware. Currently, Democrats hold all positions of authority in Delaware, as well as majorities in the state Senate and House. The Democrats have held the governorship since 1993, having won the last seven gubernatorial elections. Democrats presently hold all the nine statewide elected offices, while the Republicans last won any statewide offices in 2014, <a href="/wiki/State_Auditor" class="mw-redirect" title="State Auditor">State Auditor</a> and <a href="/wiki/State_Treasurer" class="mw-redirect" title="State Treasurer">State Treasurer</a>.</p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/First_Party_System" title="First Party System">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Party_System" title="Second Party System">Second Party Systems</a>, Delaware was a stronghold for the <a href="/wiki/Federalist_Party" title="Federalist Party">Federalist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whig_Party_(United_States)" title="Whig Party (United States)">Whig</a> Parties, respectively. After a relatively brief adherence to the Democratic Solid South following the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">US Civil War</a>, Delaware became a Republican-leaning state from <a href="/wiki/1896_United_States_presidential_election" title="1896 United States presidential election">1896</a> through <a href="/wiki/1948_United_States_presidential_election" title="1948 United States presidential election">1948</a>, voting for losing Republicans <a href="/wiki/Charles_Evans_Hughes" title="Charles Evans Hughes">Charles Evans Hughes</a> in <a href="/wiki/1916_United_States_presidential_election" title="1916 United States presidential election">1916</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Hoover" title="Herbert Hoover">Herbert Hoover</a> in <a href="/wiki/1932_United_States_presidential_election" title="1932 United States presidential election">1932</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_E._Dewey" title="Thomas E. Dewey">Thomas Dewey</a> in 1948.</p>
      <p>During the second half of the 20th century, Delaware was a bellwether state, voting for the winner of every presidential election from <a href="/wiki/1952_United_States_presidential_election" title="1952 United States presidential election">1952</a> through <a href="/wiki/1996_United_States_presidential_election" title="1996 United States presidential election">1996</a>. Delaware's bellwether status came to an end when Delaware voted for <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a> in <a href="/wiki/2000_United_States_presidential_election" title="2000 United States presidential election">2000</a> by 13%. Subsequent elections have continued to demonstrate Delaware's current strong Democratic lean: <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> carried the First State by 8% in <a href="/wiki/2004_United_States_presidential_election" title="2004 United States presidential election">2004</a>; <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> carried it by 25% and by 19% in his two elections of <a href="/wiki/2008_United_States_presidential_election" title="2008 United States presidential election">2008</a> and <a href="/wiki/2012_United_States_presidential_election" title="2012 United States presidential election">2012</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> carried it by 11% as she lost the Electoral College in <a href="/wiki/2016_United_States_presidential_election" title="2016 United States presidential election">2016</a>. In 2020, Delaware native (and Barack Obama's former Vice President and running mate) Joe Biden headed the Democratic ticket; he carried his home state by just shy of 19% en route to a national 4.5% win.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup></p>
      <p>The dominant factor in Delaware's political shift has been the strong Democratic trend in heavily urbanized <a href="/wiki/New_Castle_County,_Delaware" title="New Castle County, Delaware">New Castle County</a>, home to 55% of Delaware's population. New Castle County has not voted Republican in a presidential election since <a href="/wiki/1988_United_States_presidential_election" title="1988 United States presidential election">1988</a>, and has given Democrats over 60% of its vote in every election from 2004 on. In 1992, 2000, 2004, and 2016, the Republican presidential candidate carried both Kent and Sussex but lost by double digits each time in New Castle County, which was a large enough margin to tip the state to the Democrats. New Castle County also elects a substantial majority of the state legislature; 27 of the 41 state house districts and 14 of the 21 state senate districts are based in New Castle County.</p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Freedom_of_information">Freedom of information</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Freedom of information">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_information_in_the_United_States#State_legislation" title="Freedom of information in the United States">Freedom of information in the United States §&nbsp;State legislation</a>
      </div>
      <p>Each of the 50 states of the United States has passed some form of freedom of information legislation, which provides a mechanism for the general public to request information of the government.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup> In 2011 Delaware passed legislation placing a 15 business day time limit on addressing freedom-of-information requests, to either produce information or an explanation of why such information would take longer than this time to produce.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup></p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxation">Taxation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Taxation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <p>Tax is collected by the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Division_of_Revenue" class="mw-redirect" title="Delaware Division of Revenue">Delaware Division of Revenue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup></p>
      <p>Delaware has six different <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a> brackets, ranging from 2.2% to 5.95%. The state does not assess <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">sales tax</a> on consumers. The state does, however, impose a tax on the gross receipts of most businesses. Business and occupational license tax rates range from 0.096% to 1.92%, depending on the category of business activity.</p>
      <p>Delaware does not assess a state-level tax on real or personal property. Real estate is subject to county <a href="/wiki/Property_tax" title="Property tax">property taxes</a>, school district property taxes, vocational school district taxes, and, if located within an incorporated area, municipal property taxes.</p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Gambling_in_the_United_States#Authorized_types" title="Gambling in the United States">Gambling</a> provides significant revenue to the state. For instance, the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Park_Racetrack#Casino" title="Delaware Park Racetrack">casino at Delaware Park Racetrack</a> provided more than $100<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>million to the state in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup></p>
      <p>In June 2018, Delaware became the first U.S. state to legalize <a href="/wiki/Sports_betting" title="Sports betting">sports betting</a> following the <a href="/wiki/Professional_and_Amateur_Sports_Protection_Act_of_1992#US_Supreme_Court_decision" title="Professional and Amateur Sports Protection Act of 1992">Supreme Court ruling to repeal the Professional and Amateur Sports Protection Act of 1992</a> (PASPA).<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup></p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Voter_registration">Voter registration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Voter registration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_entertainment">Culture and entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Culture and entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Delaware_festivals" title="Delaware festivals">Delaware festivals</a>
      </div>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
