      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2017_Apache_Warrior_400_from_turn_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/2017_Apache_Warrior_400_from_turn_1.jpg/220px-2017_Apache_Warrior_400_from_turn_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/2017_Apache_Warrior_400_from_turn_1.jpg/330px-2017_Apache_Warrior_400_from_turn_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/2017_Apache_Warrior_400_from_turn_1.jpg/440px-2017_Apache_Warrior_400_from_turn_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2017_Apache_Warrior_400_from_turn_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>NASCAR racing at Dover International Speedway
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>As Delaware has no franchises in the major American professional sports leagues, many Delawareans follow either <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Philadelphia" title="Sports in Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> or <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Baltimore" title="Sports in Baltimore">Baltimore</a> teams. In the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_National_Basketball_Association" title="Women's National Basketball Association">WNBA</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Mystics" title="Washington Mystics">Washington Mystics</a> enjoy a major following due to the presence of Wilmington native and University of Delaware product <a href="/wiki/Elena_Delle_Donne" title="Elena Delle Donne">Elena Delle Donne</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Fightin%27_Blue_Hens_football" title="Delaware Fightin' Blue Hens football">University of Delaware's football team</a> has a large following throughout the state, with the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_State_Hornets_football" title="Delaware State Hornets football">Delaware State University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wesley_College_(Delaware)" title="Wesley College (Delaware)">Wesley College</a> teams also enjoying a smaller degree of support.</p>
      <p>Delaware is home to <a href="/wiki/Dover_International_Speedway" title="Dover International Speedway">Dover International Speedway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dover_Downs" title="Dover Downs">Dover Downs</a>. DIS, also known as the <i>Monster Mile</i>, is one of only 10 tracks in the nation to have hosted 100 or more <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> Cup Series races. Dover Downs is a popular <a href="/wiki/Harness_racing" title="Harness racing">harness racing</a> facility. It is the only co-located horse- and car-racing facility in the nation, with the Dover Downs track located inside the DIS track.</p>
      <p>Delaware is represented in <a href="/wiki/USA_Rugby_League" title="USA Rugby League">rugby</a> by the Delaware Black Foxes, a 2015 expansion club.</p>
      <p>Delaware has been home to <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling" title="Professional wrestling">professional wrestling</a> outfit <a href="/wiki/Combat_Zone_Wrestling" title="Combat Zone Wrestling">Combat Zone Wrestling</a> (CZW). CZW has been affiliated with the annual Tournament of Death and <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Wrestling_Association" title="East Coast Wrestling Association">ECWA</a> with its annual <a href="/wiki/ECWA_Super_8_Tournament" title="ECWA Super 8 Tournament">Super<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>8 Tournament</a>.</p>
      <p>Delaware's official state sport is <a href="/wiki/Bicycling" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicycling">bicycling</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup></p>
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_state">Sister state</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Sister state">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
      <p>Delaware's <a href="/wiki/Paradiplomacy#United_States" title="Paradiplomacy">sister state</a> in Japan is <a href="/wiki/Miyagi_Prefecture" title="Miyagi Prefecture">Miyagi Prefecture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup></p>
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Delawareans">Delawareans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Delawareans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Delaware" title="List of people from Delaware">List of people from Delaware</a>
      </div>
      <p>Prominent Delawareans include the <a href="/wiki/Du_Pont_family" title="Du Pont family">du Pont family</a> of politicians and businesspersons and the <a href="/wiki/Biden_family" class="mw-redirect" title="Biden family">Biden family</a> among whom <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a> is notable as the 46th and current president of the United States.</p>

         <li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.bls.gov/regions/mid-atlantic/">"Mid-Atlantic Home&nbsp;: Mid–Atlantic Information Office&nbsp;: U.S. Bureau of Labor Statistics"</a>. <i>www.bls.gov</i>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20190408092405/https://www.bls.gov/regions/mid-atlantic/">Archived</a> from the original on April 8, 2019<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">July 27,</span> 2017</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=www.bls.gov&amp;rft.atitle=Mid-Atlantic+Home+%3A+Mid%E2%80%93Atlantic+Information+Office+%3A+U.S.+Bureau+of+Labor+Statistics&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.bls.gov%2Fregions%2Fmid-atlantic%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ADelaware" class="Z3988"></span></span></li>
         <li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.etymonline.com/index.php?term=Delaware">"Delaware"</a>. <i>Online Etymology Dictionary</i>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20071012121643/http://etymonline.com/index.php?term=Delaware">Archived</a> from the original on October 12, 2007<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">February 24,</span> 2007</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Delaware&amp;rft.btitle=Online+Etymology+Dictionary&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.etymonline.com%2Findex.php%3Fterm%3DDelaware&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ADelaware" class="Z3988"></span></span></li>
         <li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"The First to Ratify" would be more accurate, as the beginnings of the states themselves date back to the Declaration of Independence, celebrated July 4, 1776, when what was to become the State of Delaware was still the three lower counties of Pennsylvania with the governor in Philadelphia, and not establishing independence from that body until <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Constitution_of_1776#Background" title="Delaware Constitution of 1776">September 20, 1776</a>. According to Delaware's own website, "Delaware became a state in 1776, just two months after the signing of the Declaration of Independence." (ref-<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://delaware.gov/facts/DelawareFactsandSymbols.pdf">pdf</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20161223143442/http://delaware.gov/facts/DelawareFactsandSymbols.pdf">Archived</a> December 23, 2016, at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>) Therefore Delaware was actually the <i>last</i> of the thirteen colonies to establish itself as a state. Additionally, the <a href="/wiki/50_State_Quarters#Designs" class="mw-redirect" title="50 State Quarters">Delaware State Quarter</a> is minted with this nickname, yet shows <a href="/wiki/Caesar_Rodney#American_Revolution" title="Caesar Rodney">Caesar Rodney</a> on horseback in commemoration of how he was the <i>last</i> delegate to show up to the Continental Congress for the historic vote for independence. And with regard to the original Articles of Confederation, Delaware was the <a href="/wiki/Articles_of_Confederation#Ratification" title="Articles of Confederation">12th of the 13 states to ratify</a>.</span></li>
